General <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masaharu_Homma" title="Masaharu Homma">Masaharu Homma</a>. About 12,000 are made prisoners. Homma will soon face criticism from his superiors over the amount of time it has taken him to reduce the Philippines, and be forced into retirement (1943).</dd>
May 6, 1942
-After a pep talk, General Stilwell and his party of 114 set out from Indaw on foot, with only 11 Jeeps to carry their supplies and any incapacitated, to reach the Indian border. He sends a last radio message which ends, "Catastrophe quite possible." The radio is then destroyed.

May 6, 1945
-German soldiers open fire on a crowd celebrating the liberation of the Netherlands in Dam Square. At the brink of peace, 120 people were badly injured and 22 pronounced dead. This date marks the last fighting for American troops in Europe.

May 7, 1941

May 7, 1942
-Vichy forces surrender Diego Suarez, the most important port in Madagascar, to British forces involved in Operation Ironclad. However, the Vichy forces are able to withdraw in good order.
-<dd> Vichy forces surrender <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diego_Suarez,_Malagasy_Republic" title="Diego Suarez, Malagasy Republic">Diego Suarez</a>, the most important port in Madagascar, to British forces involved in <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Ironclad" title="Operation Ironclad">Operation Ironclad</a>. However, the Vichy forces are able to withdraw in good order.</dd>
May 7, 1942
-In the Coral Sea, Japanese search planes spot refueling ship USS Neosho and destroyer USS Sims, which have retired from Fletcher's Task Force 17 into what should have been safer waters to refuel Sims. They are mistaken for an aircraft carrier and a cruiser. Japanese Admiral Takagi, believing he has at last found the location of Fletcher's main force, orders a full out attack by carriers Shōkaku and Zuikaku and sinks both ships. This distraction helps prevent the Japanese from finding the real location of Fletcher's carriers. Meanwhile, Fletcher has a similar false alarm, the spotting of two cruisers and two destroyers being mistakenly encrypted as "two carriers and four cruisers." By chance, though, planes from USS Lexington and USS Yorktown stumble across light carrier Shōhō while pursuing the false lead and sink her, leading to the first use in the American Navy of the signal, "Scratch one flattop." Admiral Inoue is so alarmed by the loss of Shōhō he halts the Port Moresby invasion group north of the Louisiades until the American carriers can be found and destroyed.
-<dd> In the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_the_Coral_Sea" title="Battle of the Coral Sea">Coral Sea</a>, Japanese search planes spot refueling ship <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USS_Neosho_(AO-23)" title="USS Neosho (AO-23)">USS <i>Neosho</i></a> and destroyer <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USS_Sims_(DD-409)" title="USS Sims (DD-409)">USS <i>Sims</i></a>, which have retired from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Jack_Fletcher" title="Frank Jack Fletcher">Fletcher's</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Task_Force_17" title="Task Force 17">Task Force 17</a> into what should have been safer waters to refuel <i>Sims</i>. They are mistaken for an aircraft carrier and a cruiser. Japanese Admiral <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Takeo_Takagi" title="Takeo Takagi">Takagi</a>, believing he has at last found the location of Fletcher's main force, orders a full out attack by carriers <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_aircraft_carrier_Sh%C5%8Dkaku" title="Japanese aircraft carrier Shōkaku"><i>Shōkaku</i></a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_aircraft_carrier_Zuikaku" title="Japanese aircraft carrier Zuikaku"><i>Zuikaku</i></a> and sinks both ships. This distraction helps prevent the Japanese from finding the real location of Fletcher's carriers. Meanwhile, Fletcher has a similar false alarm, the spotting of two cruisers and two destroyers being mistakenly encrypted as "two carriers and four cruisers." By chance, though, planes from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USS_Lexington_(CV-2)" title="USS Lexington (CV-2)">USS <i>Lexington</i></a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USS_Yorktown_(CV-5)" title="USS Yorktown (CV-5)">USS <i>Yorktown</i></a> stumble across light carrier <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_aircraft_carrier_Sh%C5%8Dh%C5%8D" title="Japanese aircraft carrier Shōhō"><i>Shōhō</i></a> while pursuing the false lead and sink her, leading to the first use in the American Navy of the signal, "Scratch one flattop." Admiral <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shigeyoshi_Inoue" title="Shigeyoshi Inoue">Inoue</a> is so alarmed by the loss of <i>Shōhō</i> he halts the Port Moresby invasion group north of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louisiade_Archipelago" title="Louisiade Archipelago">Louisiades</a> until the American carriers can be found and destroyed.</dd>
May 7, 1942
-In Burma, General Stilwell must abandon his Jeeps. From here on all in the party will have to march. The fifty-nine-year-old General decides a cadence of one hundred five beats per minute will best match the disparate abilities of his party, and they march fifty minutes and rest ten each hour.
-<dd> In Burma, General <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stilwell" title="Joseph Stilwell">Stilwell</a> must abandon his Jeeps. From here on all in the party will have to march. The fifty-nine-year-old General decides a cadence of one hundred five beats per minute will best match the disparate abilities of his party, and they march fifty minutes and rest ten each hour.</dd>
May 7, 1943
-Tunis captured by British First Army. Meanwhile the Americans take Bizerte.
-<dd> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a> captured by British First Army. Meanwhile the Americans take Bizerte.</dd>
May 7, 1945
-Germany surrenders unconditionally to the Allies at the Western Allied Headquarters in Rheims, France at 241 a.m. In accordance with orders from Reich President Karl Dönitz, General Alfred Jodl signs for Germany.  Hermann Göring, for a while in the hands of the SS, surrenders to the Americans. Elements of Task Force Smythe, U.S. 80th ID in Austria, fire last American shots of the war in Europe when 80th Recon Platoon is strafed by 2 German planes and returns fire causing one plane to leave trailing smoke.
-<dd> Germany surrenders unconditionally to the Allies at the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Headquarters_Allied_Expeditionary_Force" title="Supreme Headquarters Allied Expeditionary Force">Western Allied Headquarters</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rheims" title="Rheims">Rheims</a>, France at 2:41 a.m. In accordance with orders from Reich President <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_D%C3%B6nitz" title="Karl Dönitz">Karl Dönitz</a>, General <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfred_Jodl" title="Alfred Jodl">Alfred Jodl</a> signs for Germany. Hermann Göring, for a while in the hands of the SS, surrenders to the Americans. Elements of Task Force Smythe, U.S. 80th ID in Austria, fire last American shots of the war in Europe when 80th Recon Platoon is strafed by 2 German planes and returns fire causing one plane to leave trailing smoke.</dd>
May 8, 1940
-Prime Minister Neville Chamberlain barely survives Norway Debate vote in the House of Commons.
-<dd> Prime Minister <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neville_Chamberlain" title="Neville Chamberlain">Neville Chamberlain</a> barely survives <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norway_Debate" title="Norway Debate">Norway Debate</a> vote in the House of Commons.</dd>
May 8, 1941
-Heavy convoy losses in the Atlantic continue; however, one U-boat (U-110) is captured by the British navy and another copy of the "Enigma" machine is discovered and saved. It will help to turn the fortunes in the Atlantic battle. Bombing of Nottingham by the Luftwaffe.
-<dd> Heavy convoy losses in the Atlantic continue; however, one U-boat (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_submarine_U-110_(1940)" title="German submarine U-110 (1940)"><i>U-110</i></a>) is captured by the British navy and another copy of the "Enigma" machine is discovered and saved. It will help to turn the fortunes in the Atlantic battle. Bombing of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nottingham" title="Nottingham">Nottingham</a> by the Luftwaffe.</dd>
May 8, 1942
-In the Coral Sea, each side finally locates the other's main carrier groups, consisting of Japanese carriers Shōkaku and Zuikaku, and American carriers Lexington and Yorktown. Several attacks follow. Only Zuikaku escapes unscathed; Shōkaku has her flight deck bent, requiring two months' repairs; Lexington is sunk and Yorktown damaged. Fletcher retires; this action closes the Battle. While arguably a stalemate or even tactical victory for the Japanese, who have sunk the most tonnage and the only large carrier, the Battle of the Coral Sea is usually seen as a strategic victory for the United States, as Admiral Inoue cancels the Port Moresby operation, the first significant failure of a Japanese strategic operation in the Pacific Theatre. In addition, Yorktown will be repaired in time to make important contributions at Midway (although she will not survive), whereas neither the damaged Shōkaku nor Zuikaku (which, although not directly attacked, has suffered unsustainable losses in aircraft), will be able to refit in time for Midway, giving the Japanese only four operable carriers available for that battle.
-<dd> In the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_the_Coral_Sea" title="Battle of the Coral Sea">Coral Sea</a>, each side finally locates the other's main carrier groups, consisting of Japanese carriers <i>Shōkaku</i> and <i>Zuikaku</i>, and American carriers <i>Lexington</i> and <i>Yorktown</i>. Several attacks follow. Only <i>Zuikaku</i> escapes unscathed; <i>Shōkaku</i> has her flight deck bent, requiring two months' repairs; <i>Lexington</i> is sunk and <i>Yorktown</i> damaged. Fletcher retires; this action closes the Battle. While arguably a stalemate or even tactical victory for the Japanese, who have sunk the most tonnage and the only large carrier, the Battle of the Coral Sea is usually seen as a strategic victory for the United States, as Admiral <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shigeyoshi_Inoue" title="Shigeyoshi Inoue">Inoue</a> cancels the Port Moresby operation, the first significant failure of a Japanese strategic operation in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">Pacific Theatre</a>. In addition, <i>Yorktown</i> will be repaired in time to make important contributions at <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Battle_of_Midway" title="The Battle of Midway">Midway</a> (although she will not survive), whereas neither the damaged <i>Shōkaku</i> nor <i>Zuikaku</i> (which, although not directly attacked, has suffered unsustainable losses in aircraft), will be able to refit in time for Midway, giving the Japanese only four operable carriers available for that battle.</dd>

May 8, 1945
-Victory in Europe Day The ceasefire takes effect at one minute past midnight. In accordance with Dönitz's orders, Colonel-General Carl Hilpert unconditionally surrenders his troops in the Courland Pocket.  Germany surrenders again unconditionally to the Soviet Union army but this time in a ceremony hosted by the Soviet Union. In accordance with orders from Dönitz, General Wilhelm Keitel signs for Germany. The remaining members of President Jozef Tiso's pro-German Slovak Republic capitulates to the American General Walton Walker's XX Corps in Kremsmünster, Austria. The Prague uprising ends with negotiated surrender with Czech resistance which allowed the Germans in Prague to leave the city. In order to disarm the Japanese in Vietnam, the Allies divide the country in half at the 16th parallel. Chinese Nationalists will move in and disarm the Japanese north of the parallel while the British will move in and do the same in the south. During the conference, representatives from France request the return of all French pre-war colonies in Indochina. Their request is granted.
-<dd> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Victory_in_Europe_Day" title="Victory in Europe Day">Victory in Europe Day</a>: The ceasefire takes effect at one minute past midnight. In accordance with Dönitz's orders, Colonel-General <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Hilpert" title="Carl Hilpert">Carl Hilpert</a> unconditionally surrenders his troops in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Courland_Pocket" title="Courland Pocket">Courland Pocket</a>. Germany surrenders again unconditionally to the Soviet Union army but this time in a ceremony hosted by the Soviet Union. In accordance with orders from Dönitz, General <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_Keitel" title="Wilhelm Keitel">Wilhelm Keitel</a> signs for Germany. The remaining members of President <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jozef_Tiso" title="Jozef Tiso">Jozef Tiso</a>'s pro-German <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slovak_Republic_(1939-1945)" title="Slovak Republic (1939-1945)">Slovak Republic</a> capitulates to the American General <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walton_Walker" title="Walton Walker">Walton Walker</a>'s <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/XX_Corps_(United_States)" title="XX Corps (United States)">XX Corps</a> in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kremsm%C3%BCnster" title="Kremsmünster">Kremsmünster</a>, Austria. The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prague_uprising" title="Prague uprising">Prague uprising</a> ends with negotiated surrender with <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czech_resistance" title="Czech resistance">Czech resistance</a> which allowed the Germans in Prague to leave the city. In order to disarm the Japanese in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, the Allies divide the country in half at the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/16th_parallel_north" title="16th parallel north">16th parallel</a>. Chinese Nationalists will move in and disarm the Japanese <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Vietnam" title="North Vietnam">north</a> of the parallel while the British will move in and do the same in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Vietnam" title="South Vietnam">south</a>. During the conference, representatives from France request the return of all French pre-war colonies in <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indochina" title="Indochina">Indochina</a>. Their request is granted.</dd>

May 9, 1942
-On the night of 8/9 May 1942, gunners of the Ceylon Garrison Artillery on Horsburgh Island in the Cocos Islands rebelled. Their mutiny was crushed and three of them were executed, the only British Commonwealth soldiers to be executed for mutiny during the Second World War.
-<dd> On the night of 8/9 May 1942, gunners of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ceylon_Garrison_Artillery" title="Ceylon Garrison Artillery">Ceylon Garrison Artillery</a> on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horsburgh_Island" title="Horsburgh Island">Horsburgh Island</a> in the Cocos Islands rebelled. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cocos_Islands_mutiny" title="Cocos Islands mutiny">Their mutiny</a> was crushed and three of them were executed, the only British Commonwealth soldiers to be executed for mutiny during the Second World War.</dd>
May 9, 1942
-USS Wasp and HMS Eagle deliver a second contingent of Spitfires to Malta in Operation Bowery. A few days later, a grateful Churchill will signal Wasp "Who says a Wasp can't sting twice?" These aircraft, employed more aggressively than those previously delivered, turn the tide in the skies over Malta during the next few days, and the Axis is forced to abandon daylight bombing. This is a major turning point in the Siege, and thus in the North African Campaign, although the approaches to the island remain subject to deadly and accurate Axis air attack, preventing efficient re-supply of the island.
-<dd> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USS_Wasp_(CV-7)" title="USS Wasp (CV-7)">USS <i>Wasp</i></a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HMS_Eagle_(1918)" title="HMS Eagle (1918)">HMS <i>Eagle</i></a> deliver a second contingent of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supermarine_Spitfire" title="Supermarine Spitfire">Spitfires</a> to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Malta_(World_War_II)" title="Siege of Malta (World War II)">Malta</a> in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Bowery" title="Operation Bowery">Operation Bowery</a>. A few days later, a grateful <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Churchill" title="Churchill">Churchill</a> will signal <i>Wasp</i> "Who says a <i>Wasp</i> can't sting twice?" These aircraft, employed more aggressively than those previously delivered, turn the tide in the skies over Malta during the next few days, and the Axis is forced to abandon daylight bombing. This is a major turning point in the Siege, and thus in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_African_Campaign" title="North African Campaign">North African Campaign</a>, although the approaches to the island remain subject to deadly and accurate Axis air attack, preventing efficient re-supply of the island.</dd>

May 10, 1940
-Germany invades Belgium, France, Luxembourg and the Netherlands; Winston Churchill becomes Prime Minister of the United Kingdom upon the resignation of Neville Chamberlain. The United Kingdom invades Iceland. Belgium declares a state of emergency. Churchill is called on to form a wartime coalition government. The massive German offensive against the Western front The invasion of Luxembourg, Belgium, the Netherlands, and France begins.  In a bold stroke, German paratroops capture the Belgian fort Eben Emael.
-<dd> Germany invades Belgium, France, Luxembourg and the Netherlands; <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> becomes <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister of the United Kingdom</a> upon the resignation of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neville_Chamberlain" title="Neville Chamberlain">Neville Chamberlain</a>. The United Kingdom <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invasion_of_Iceland" title="Invasion of Iceland">invades Iceland</a>. Belgium declares a state of emergency. Churchill is called on to form a wartime coalition government. The massive German offensive against the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Western Front (World War II)">Western front</a>: The invasion of Luxembourg, Belgium, the Netherlands, and France begins.  In a bold stroke, German paratroops <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Eben-Emael" title="Battle of Fort Eben-Emael">capture</a> the Belgian fort <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eben_Emael" title="Eben Emael">Eben Emael</a>.</dd>

May 10, 1941
-Rudolf Hess is captured in Scotland after bailing out of his plane; his self-appointed mission was to make peace with the United Kingdom. The United Kingdom's House of Commons is damaged by the Luftwaffe in an air raid. Other targets are Hull, Liverpool, Belfast, and the shipbuilding area of the River Clyde in Scotland. This is close to the end of the Blitz, as Germany shifts its focus toward Soviet Union and the East.
-<dd> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rudolf_Hess" title="Rudolf Hess">Rudolf Hess</a> is captured in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> after bailing out of his plane; his self-appointed mission was to make peace with the United Kingdom. The United Kingdom's <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" title="British House of Commons">House of Commons</a> is damaged by the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a> in an <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airstrike" title="Airstrike">air raid</a>. Other targets are Hull, Liverpool, Belfast, and the shipbuilding area of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/River_Clyde" title="River Clyde">River Clyde</a> in Scotland. This is close to the end of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz">the Blitz</a>, as Germany shifts its focus toward Soviet Union and the East.</dd>

May 10, 1942
-Churchill, growing ever more frustrated with General Auchinleck's inactivity, finally sends him a telegram with a clear order; attack in time to cover for the Harpoon/Vigorous convoys to Malta during the dark of the moon in early June. This places Auchinleck in the position of complying or resigning. Auchinleck does not immediately reply, leaving Churchill, CIGS, and the War Cabinet in a state of suspense.
-<dd> <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Churchill" title="Churchill">Churchill</a>, growing ever more frustrated with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Claude_Auchinleck" title="Claude Auchinleck">General Auchinleck's</a> inactivity, finally sends him a telegram with a clear order; attack in time to cover for the Harpoon/Vigorous convoys to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Malta_(World_War_II)" title="Siege of Malta (World War II)">Malta</a> during the dark of the moon in early June. This places Auchinleck in the position of complying or resigning. Auchinleck does not immediately reply, leaving Churchill, <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_of_the_Imperial_General_Staff" title="Chief of the Imperial General Staff">CIGS</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Churchill_War_Ministry" title="Churchill War Ministry">War Cabinet</a> in a state of suspense.</dd>

May 12, 1942
-Second Battle of Kharkov – In the eastern Ukraine, Soviet forces of Marshal Timoshenko's Southwest Theatre of Operations, including Gorodnyanski's 6th Army and Kharitonov's 9th Army, initiate a major offensive to capture Kharkov from the Germans. 9th Army is to attack first, with a primary objective of Krasnograd, and a secondary one of Poltava; 6th Army is to follow immediately. After 9th Army has captured Krasnograd, 6th Army is to swing north and link up with 28th Army and 57th Army, the latter two formations having meanwhile cut the railway between Belgorad and Kharkov.
-<dd> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Kharkov" title="Second Battle of Kharkov">Second Battle of Kharkov</a> – In the eastern <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> forces of Marshal <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semyon_Timoshenko" title="Semyon Timoshenko">Timoshenko's</a> Southwest Theatre of Operations, including Gorodnyanski's <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/6th_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="6th Army (Soviet Union)">6th Army</a> and Kharitonov's <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/9th_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="9th Army (Soviet Union)">9th Army</a>, initiate a major offensive to capture <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kharkov" title="Kharkov">Kharkov</a> from the Germans. 9th Army is to attack first, with a primary objective of Krasnograd, and a secondary one of Poltava; 6th Army is to follow immediately. After 9th Army has captured Krasnograd, 6th Army is to swing north and link up with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/28th_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="28th Army (Soviet Union)">28th Army</a> and 57th Army, the latter two formations having meanwhile cut the railway between Belgorad and Kharkov.</dd>

May 13, 1941
-Yugoslav Army Colonel Draža Mihailović summons up the "Yugoslav Army in the Fatherland" which mostly consists of Serbs, but also includes Slovenes, Bosnians, and Croats. Mihailović treks from Bosnia to Ravna Gora in central Serbia, and issues an uprising call promising a struggle against the occupiers and the restoration of the Yugoslavian Monarchy. At this point, Josip Broz Tito and the Yugoslav Partisans are aligned with the Soviet Union, which is still friendly with Germany. The bulk of the German "Flyer Command Iraq" (Fliegerführer Irak) arrives in Mosul to support the Iraqi government of Rashid Ali.
-<dd> Yugoslav Army Colonel <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dra%C5%BEa_Mihailovi%C4%87" title="Draža Mihailović">Draža Mihailović</a> summons up the "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chetniks" title="Chetniks">Yugoslav Army in the Fatherland</a>" which mostly consists of Serbs, but also includes Slovenes, Bosnians, and Croats. Mihailović treks from Bosnia to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ravna_Gora_(highland)" title="Ravna Gora (highland)">Ravna Gora</a> in central Serbia, and issues an uprising call promising a struggle against the occupiers and the restoration of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavian Monarchy</a>. At this point, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Josip Broz Tito</a> and the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yugoslav_Partisans" title="Yugoslav Partisans">Yugoslav Partisans</a> are aligned with the Soviet Union, which is still friendly with Germany. The bulk of the German "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fliegerf%C3%BChrer_Irak" title="Fliegerführer Irak">Flyer Command Iraq</a>" (<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fliegerf%C3%BChrer_Irak" title="Fliegerführer Irak">Fliegerführer Irak</a></i>) arrives in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mosul" title="Mosul">Mosul</a> to support the Iraqi government of Rashid Ali.</dd>

May 14, 1940
-The creation of the Local Defence Volunteers (the Home Guard) is announced by the new Secretary of State for War Anthony Eden. It is mostly composed of the elderly and retired. Churchill asks President Roosevelt and Canada for aid in these dark days.  Outlines of the new British coalition, which includes Labour, Liberal, and Conservative members, is made public.
-<dd> The creation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Local_Defence_Volunteers" title="Local Defence Volunteers">Local Defence Volunteers</a> (the <i>Home Guard</i>) is announced by the new <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_War" title="Secretary of State for War">Secretary of State for War</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthony_Eden" title="Anthony Eden">Anthony Eden</a>. May 14, 1942
-In response to the Soviet offensive in the Kharkov area, Hitler orders elements of Richthofen's Fliegerkorps VIII north to do ground support missions. As a result, by the end of the day 14 May, the Germans have established a tentative but increasing air superiority over the Kharkov sector. In addition, on this day Hitler orders General Kleist, whose command is in positions opposite and to the south of the Soviets' left flank, to quickly prepare and launch a strong armoured counter-offensive.
-<dd> In response to the Soviet offensive in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Kharkov" title="Second Battle of Kharkov">Kharkov</a> area, <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hitler" title="Hitler">Hitler</a> orders elements of <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wolfram_von_Richthofen" title="Wolfram von Richthofen">Richthofen's</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/8th_Air_Corps_(Germany)" title="8th Air Corps (Germany)"><i>Fliegerkorps VIII</i></a> north to do ground support missions. As a result, by the end of the day 14 May, the Germans have established a tentative but increasing air superiority over the Kharkov sector. In addition, on this day Hitler orders <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Ludwig_Ewald_von_Kleist" title="Paul Ludwig Ewald von Kleist">General Kleist</a>, whose command is in positions opposite and to the south of the Soviets' left flank, to quickly prepare and launch a strong armoured counter-offensive.</dd>

May 15, 1940
-The capitulation of the Dutch army is signed. In a response to the Rotterdam Blitz, the first large-scale strategic bombing of World War II targets Gelsenkirchen, followed by Hamburg, Bremen, Cologne, Essen, Duisburg, Düsseldorf and Hanover during the next days. German forces cross over the Meuse River.
-<dd> The capitulation of the Dutch army is signed. May 16, 1943
-The Warsaw Ghetto Uprising ends. The ghetto has been destroyed, with about 14,000 Jews killed and about another 40,000 sent to the death camps at Majdanek and Treblinka. The Dambuster Raids are carried out by RAF 617 Squadron on two German dams, Mohne and Eder. The Ruhr war industries lose electrical power.
-<dd> The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising" title="Warsaw Ghetto Uprising">Warsaw Ghetto Uprising</a> ends. The ghetto has been destroyed, with about 14,000 Jews killed and about another 40,000 sent to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_camps" title="Death camps">death camps</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Majdanek" title="Majdanek">Majdanek</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treblinka" title="Treblinka">Treblinka</a>. The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Chastise" title="Operation Chastise">Dambuster Raids</a> are carried out by RAF 617 Squadron on two German dams, Mohne and Eder. The Ruhr war industries lose electrical power.</dd>

May 17, 1942
-In the salient north of Kharkov, Russian 28th and 57th Armies are having trouble making progress against General Paulus's (German) 6th Army.
-<dd> In the salient north of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Kharkov" title="Second Battle of Kharkov">Kharkov</a>, Russian <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/28th_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="28th Army (Soviet Union)">28th</a> and 57th Armies are having trouble making progress against <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedrich_Paulus" title="Friedrich Paulus">General Paulus's</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/6th_Army_(Wehrmacht)" title="6th Army (Wehrmacht)">(German) 6th Army</a>.</dd>
May 17, 1942
-For once, Adolf Hitler has not hobbled his local commander with a strict "no retreat" order, and Paulus is free to conduct an efficient delaying action. In addition, Paulus' troops are largely up to strength and fully equipped as a result of preparations for the upcoming drive to Stalingrad. In the south salient, Kharitonov's 9th Army has routed the Romanian (3rd and/or 4th Army; accounts differ) troops in his path and captured Krasnograd, and is proceeding to Poltava; Gorodnyanski's 6th Army has made its planned turn to the north to link up with 28th and 57th Armies. 9th Army's impetus has stretched Kharitonov's armoured units out along a seventy-mile track, diluting their strength; and attempts to cover his left flank by driving the Germans back from it have been unsuccessful. The Russians take only a few prisoners along this flank, but Timoshenko is dismayed by the variety of units, especially armoured units, this handful of men represent (this is because Kleist is concentrating troops in this area in preparation for his counter-offensive). Timoshenko loses confidence and has his Political Officer Nikita Khrushchev ring up the Stavka and ask for permission to halt while he secures his left flank; Stavka refuses.
-<dd> For once, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> has not hobbled his local commander with a strict "no retreat" order, and Paulus is free to conduct an efficient delaying action. In addition, Paulus' troops are largely up to strength and fully equipped as a result of preparations for the upcoming drive to Stalingrad. In the south salient, Kharitonov's <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/9th_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="9th Army (Soviet Union)">9th Army</a> has routed the Romanian (3rd and/or 4th Army; accounts differ) troops in his path and captured <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Krasnograd" title="Krasnograd">Krasnograd</a>, and is proceeding to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poltava" title="Poltava">Poltava</a>; Gorodnyanski's <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/6th_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="6th Army (Soviet Union)">6th Army</a> has made its planned turn to the north to link up with 28th and 57th Armies. 9th Army's impetus has stretched Kharitonov's armoured units out along a seventy-mile track, diluting their strength; and attempts to cover his left flank by driving the Germans back from it have been unsuccessful. The Russians take only a few prisoners along this flank, but <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semyon_Timoshenko" title="Semyon Timoshenko">Timoshenko</a> is dismayed by the variety of units, especially armoured units, this handful of men represent (this is because <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Ludwig_Ewald_von_Kleist" title="Paul Ludwig Ewald von Kleist">Kleist</a> is concentrating troops in this area in preparation for his counter-offensive). Timoshenko loses confidence and has his Political Officer <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> ring up the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stavka" title="Stavka">Stavka</a> and ask for permission to halt while he secures his left flank; Stavka refuses.</dd>
May 17, 1942
-It has been a week since Churchill sent his ultimatum to General Auchinleck, and he has not yet received a reply. He sends a terse follow-up "It is necessary for me to have some account of your general intentions in light of our recent telegrams." Again there is no immediate reply.
-<dd> It has been a week since <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Churchill</a> sent his ultimatum to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Claude_Auchinleck" title="Claude Auchinleck">General Auchinleck</a>, and he has not yet received a reply. He sends a terse follow-up: "It is necessary for me to have some account of your general intentions in light of our recent telegrams." Again there is no immediate reply.</dd>

May 18, 1942
-In the salient north of Kharkov, the Soviet offensive has bogged down. In the southern salient, Kleist has launched his counter-offensive. It is immediately successful and by the end of the first day the leading elements have reached the confluence of the Oksol and Donetz rivers, greatly narrowing the base of the salient. In the process the Germans traverse and disrupt so many lines of communication that Kharitonov's 9th Army begins to lose cohesion as a fighting force, and becomes useless as a screen to protect Gorodnyanski's 6th Army which, because of its northward progress, is badly disposed to repel the German attacks coming from the south.
-<dd> In the salient north of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Kharkov" title="Second Battle of Kharkov">Kharkov</a>, the Soviet offensive has bogged down. In the southern salient, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Ludwig_Ewald_von_Kleist" title="Paul Ludwig Ewald von Kleist">Kleist</a> has launched his counter-offensive. It is immediately successful and by the end of the first day the leading elements have reached the confluence of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oskol_River" title="Oskol River">Oksol</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donetz" title="Donetz">Donetz</a> rivers, greatly narrowing the base of the salient. In the process the Germans traverse and disrupt so many lines of communication that Kharitonov's <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/9th_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="9th Army (Soviet Union)">9th Army</a> begins to lose cohesion as a fighting force, and becomes useless as a screen to protect Gorodnyanski's <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/6th_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="6th Army (Soviet Union)">6th Army</a> which, because of its northward progress, is badly disposed to repel the German attacks coming from the south.</dd>

-<dd> The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assam_Rifles" title="Assam Rifles">Assam Rifles</a> give General <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stilwell" title="Joseph Stilwell">Stilwell's</a> party a formal salute in honor of their arrival at <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukhrul" title="Ukhrul">Ukhrul</a>, but can offer no motorized transport; the nearest road passable by trucks is still a day's march away, and there are no Jeeps yet in this part of India.</dd>
May 18, 1944
-The Battle of Monte Cassino ends in Allied victory. Polish troops of the 2nd Polish Corps led by general Władysław Anders capture  Monte Cassino. German troops in west Italy have withdrawn to the Hitler Line.  Allied troops take airfields at Myitkyina, Burma, an important air base; the struggle over the city itself will continue for nearly three months. The last Japanese resistance in the Admiralty Islands, off New Guinea comes to an end.
-<dd> The Battle of Monte Cassino ends in Allied victory. Polish troops of the 2nd Polish Corps led by general Władysław Anders capture  Monte Cassino. German troops in west Italy have withdrawn to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hitler_Line" title="Hitler Line">Hitler Line</a>. Allied troops take airfields at Myitkyina, Burma, an important air base; the struggle over the city itself will continue for nearly three months. The last Japanese resistance in the Admiralty Islands, off New Guinea comes to an end.</dd>

May 19, 1942
-At Kharkov, Kleist's counter-offensive continues to prosper; and now Paulus launches a second counter-attack from the north, designed to link up with Kleist's and encircle as many Soviet troops as possible. The Stavka, gradually becoming aware of the extent of the danger, orders Gorodnyanski's 6th Army to halt their advance. But by now Timoshenko is planning to extricate what forces he can before the two German spearheads link up.
-<dd> At <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Kharkov" title="Second Battle of Kharkov">Kharkov</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Ludwig_Ewald_von_Kleist" title="Paul Ludwig Ewald von Kleist">Kleist</a>'s counter-offensive continues to prosper; and now <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedrich_Paulus" title="Friedrich Paulus">Paulus</a> launches a second counter-attack from the north, designed to link up with Kleist's and encircle as many Soviet troops as possible. The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stavka" title="Stavka">Stavka</a>, gradually becoming aware of the extent of the danger, orders Gorodnyanski's <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/6th_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="6th Army (Soviet Union)">6th Army</a> to halt their advance. But by now <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semyon_Timoshenko" title="Semyon Timoshenko">Timoshenko</a> is planning to extricate what forces he can before the two German spearheads link up.</dd>
May 19, 1942
-General Stilwell and his party at last reach the truck roadhead at Litan; by this time the monsoon rains have started.
-<dd> General <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stilwell" title="Joseph Stilwell">Stilwell</a> and his party at last reach the truck roadhead at Litan; by this time the monsoon rains have started.</dd>
May 19, 1942
-General Auchinleck at last replies to Churchill's somewhat urgent telegram of the 10th, saying he will have an attack ready by the sailing of the Harpoon/Vigorous convoys for Malta.
-<dd> General <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Claude_Auchinleck" title="Claude Auchinleck">Auchinleck</a> at last replies to Churchill's somewhat urgent telegram of the 10th, saying he will have an attack ready by the sailing of the Harpoon/Vigorous convoys for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Malta_(World_War_II)" title="Siege of Malta (World War II)">Malta</a>.</dd>
May 19, 1943
-Winston Churchill addresses a joint session of the U.S. Congress. He praises the partnership of the two Allies.

May 20, 1940
-General Guderian's Panzer groups take Abbeville, threatening Allied forces in the area.
-<dd> General Guderian's Panzer groups take <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbeville" title="Abbeville">Abbeville</a>, threatening Allied forces in the area.</dd>
May 20, 1941
-German paratroopers land on Crete; the battle for Crete will continue for seven days. The German military mission to Iraq, Special Staff F (Sonderstab F), is created to support of "The Arab Freedom Movement in the Middle East". Sonderstab F is to include Fliegerführer Irak and other elements already in Iraq.
-<dd> German paratroopers <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Crete" title="Battle of Crete">land on Crete</a>; the battle for Crete will continue for seven days. The German military mission to Iraq, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_Staff_F" title="Special Staff F">Special Staff F</a> (<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_Staff_F" title="Special Staff F">Sonderstab F</a></i>), is created to support of "The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_nationalism" title="Arab nationalism">Arab Freedom Movement</a> in the Middle East". <i>Sonderstab F</i> is to include <i>Fliegerführer Irak</i> and other elements already in Iraq.</dd>
May 20, 1942
-The Japanese conquest of Burma is complete; it is called a "military catastrophe". Coincidentally, on this same day General Stilwell arrives in Imphal and dismisses his evacuation party. All 114 have arrived, although some have to be hospitalized due to exhaustion; one of whom, Major Frank Merrill, later commander of Merrill's Marauders, is diagnosed to have had a mild heart attack en route.
-<dd> The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_conquest_of_Burma" title="Japanese conquest of Burma">Japanese conquest of Burma</a> is complete; it is called a "military catastrophe". Coincidentally, on this same day General <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stilwell" title="Joseph Stilwell">Stilwell</a> arrives in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imphal" title="Imphal">Imphal</a> and dismisses his evacuation party. All 114 have arrived, although some have to be hospitalized due to exhaustion; one of whom, Major <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Merrill" title="Frank Merrill">Frank Merrill</a>, later commander of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Merrill%27s_Marauders" title="Merrill's Marauders">Merrill's Marauders</a>, is diagnosed to have had a mild heart attack en route.</dd>
May 20, 1942
-At Kharkov, as Kleist's and Paulus' forward elements draw ever closer together, Timoshenko sends his subordinate General Kostenko into the salient to organize a fighting retreat, or, failing that, maximize what can be saved.
-<dd> At <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Kharkov" title="Second Battle of Kharkov">Kharkov</a>, as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Ludwig_Ewald_von_Kleist" title="Paul Ludwig Ewald von Kleist">Kleist</a>'s and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedrich_Paulus" title="Friedrich Paulus">Paulus'</a> forward elements draw ever closer together, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semyon_Timoshenko" title="Semyon Timoshenko">Timoshenko</a> sends his subordinate General Kostenko into the salient to organize a fighting retreat, or, failing that, maximize what can be saved.</dd>

-The Georgian Uprising of Texel ends, concluding all World War II conflicts in the Netherlands.

May 21, 1941
-The US merchantman SS Robin Moor is sunk by German submarine U-69. The incident startles the nation, and President Roosevelt shortly announces an "unlimited national emergency." The Italian Viceroy in Ethiopia surrenders. Remnants of Italian troops keep on fighting.
-<dd> The US merchantman <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SS_Robin_Moor" title="SS Robin Moor">SS <i>Robin Moor</i></a> is sunk by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_submarine_U-69_(1940)" title="German submarine U-69 (1940)">German submarine <i>U-69</i></a>. Remnants of Italian troops keep on fighting.</dd>
May 21, 1942
-Invasion of Malta postponed indefinitely.

May 21, 1942
-In discussions with Winston Churchill and Anthony Eden, Molotov continues to press Soviet demands for territorial acquisitions made during the run-up to war, including the Baltic states, Eastern Poland, and Bessarabia. Churchill cannot or will not agree to these demands, and the talks become deadlocked.
-<dd> In discussions with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthony_Eden" title="Anthony Eden">Anthony Eden</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vyacheslav_Molotov" title="Vyacheslav Molotov">Molotov</a> continues to press Soviet demands for territorial acquisitions made during the run-up to war, including the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a>, Eastern <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a>. Churchill cannot or will not agree to these demands, and the talks become deadlocked.</dd>

May 21, 1945

May 23, 1942
-Kleist's and Paulus' tanks meet up at Balakleya, southeast of Kharkov, encircling most of the Soviets' 6th and 9th Armies.
-<dd> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Ludwig_Ewald_von_Kleist" title="Paul Ludwig Ewald von Kleist">Kleist</a>'s and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedrich_Paulus" title="Friedrich Paulus">Paulus'</a> tanks meet up at <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balakleya" title="Balakleya">Balakleya</a>, southeast of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Kharkov" title="Second Battle of Kharkov">Kharkov</a>, encircling most of the Soviets' <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/6th_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="6th Army (Soviet Union)">6th</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/9th_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="9th Army (Soviet Union)">9th Armies</a>.</dd>
May 23, 1942
-At the high-level Soviet/United Kingdom talks in London, Anthony Eden suggests abandoning attempts to reach territorial understandings, and instead conclude a twenty-years' alliance. Molotov, whose diplomatic position is weakening rapidly as the Soviet military situation deteriorates at Kerch and Kharkov, expresses interest.
-<dd> At the high-level Soviet/United Kingdom talks in London, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthony_Eden" title="Anthony Eden">Anthony Eden</a> suggests abandoning attempts to reach territorial understandings, and instead conclude a twenty-years' alliance. Molotov, whose diplomatic position is weakening rapidly as the Soviet military situation deteriorates at <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_the_Kerch_Peninsula" title="Battle of the Kerch Peninsula">Kerch</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Kharkov" title="Second Battle of Kharkov">Kharkov</a>, expresses interest.</dd>
May 23, 1944
-Allies start a new breakout from Anzio.
-<dd> Allies start a new breakout from Anzio.</dd>
May 23, 1945
-British forces capture and arrest the members of what was left of the Flensburg government. This was the German government formed by Reich President Karl Dönitz after the suicides of both Adolf Hitler and Joseph Goebbels. Heavy bombing of Yokohama, an important port and naval base. Heinrich Himmler, head of the notorious SS, dies of suicide via cyanide pill.
-<dd> British forces capture and arrest the members of what was left of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flensburg_government" title="Flensburg government">Flensburg government</a>. This was the German government formed by Reich President Karl Dönitz after the suicides of both <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> and Joseph Goebbels. Heavy bombing of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yokohama" title="Yokohama">Yokohama</a>, an important port and naval base. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heinrich_Himmler" title="Heinrich Himmler">Heinrich Himmler</a>, head of the notorious SS, dies of suicide via cyanide pill.</dd>
May 24, 1940
-The British make a final decision to cease operations in Norway.

May 24, 1941
-British battlecruiser HMS Hood is sunk by a powerful salvo from German battleship Bismarck in the North Atlantic. The Greek government leaves Crete for Cairo.
-<dd> British battlecruiser <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HMS_Hood_(51)" title="HMS Hood (51)">HMS <i>Hood</i></a> is sunk by a powerful salvo from German battleship <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_battleship_Bismarck" title="German battleship Bismarck"><i>Bismarck</i></a> in the North Atlantic. The Greek government leaves Crete for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>.</dd>
May 24, 1943
-Admiral Karl Dönitz orders the majority of U-boats to withdraw from the Atlantic because of heavy losses to new Allied anti-sub tactics. By the end of the month, 43 U-boats are lost, compared to 34 Allied ships sunk. This is referred to as "Black May". Josef Mengele becomes Chief Medical Officer in Auschwitz.
-<dd> Admiral <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_D%C3%B6nitz" title="Karl Dönitz">Karl Dönitz</a> orders the majority of U-boats to withdraw from the Atlantic because of heavy losses to new Allied <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-submarine_weapon#World_War_II" title="Anti-submarine weapon">anti-sub tactics</a>. By the end of the month, 43 U-boats are lost, compared to 34 Allied ships sunk. This is referred to as "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_May_(1943)" title="Black May (1943)">Black May</a>". <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josef_Mengele" title="Josef Mengele">Josef Mengele</a> becomes Chief Medical Officer in <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auschwitz" title="Auschwitz">Auschwitz</a>.</dd>
May 25, 1940
-The Allied forces, British and French alike, retreat to Dunkirk. Hitler orders a halt to the advance of Germans toward the Allied beachhead and allows Hermann Göring to use the Luftwaffe to attack.  British R.A.F. defends the beachhead. Sporadic Luftwaffe bombings in England. Boulogne-sur-Mer surrenders to the Germans.
-<dd> The Allied forces, British and French alike, retreat to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dunkirk" title="Dunkirk">Dunkirk</a>. Hitler orders a halt to the advance of Germans toward the Allied beachhead and allows Hermann Göring to use the Luftwaffe to attack.  British R.A.F. defends the beachhead. Sporadic Luftwaffe bombings in England. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boulogne-sur-Mer" title="Boulogne-sur-Mer">Boulogne-sur-Mer</a> surrenders to the Germans.</dd>
May 25, 1940
-Soviet Union is preparing a total takeover in the Baltic States organizing and staging conflicts between the Baltic States and the USSR. Soviet government accuses Lithuania of kidnapping Soviet soldiers.
-<dd> Soviet Union is preparing a total takeover in the Baltic States organizing and staging conflicts between the Baltic States and the USSR. Soviet government accuses Lithuania of kidnapping Soviet soldiers.</dd>

-[25-28] 86 Belgian civilians are murdered by German forces in the village of Vinkt.

May 25, 1942
-In preparation for the next battle, the Japanese naval strategists send diversionary forces to the Aleutians.
-<dd> In preparation for the next battle, the Japanese naval strategists send diversionary forces to the Aleutians.</dd>
May 25, 1944
-Allies at Anzio link up with Allies from south Italy. Though Harold Alexander wishes to trap the German Tenth Army, American Fifth Army commander Mark W. Clark orders Truscott to turn north toward Rome. The Germans in Italy form a new defensive position on the Caesar C line.
-<dd> Allies at Anzio link up with Allies from south Italy. Though Harold Alexander wishes to trap the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/10th_Army_(Wehrmacht)" title="10th Army (Wehrmacht)">German Tenth Army</a>, American <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Army_North" title="United States Army North">Fifth Army</a> commander <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_W._Clark" title="Mark W. Clark">Mark W. Clark</a> orders Truscott to turn north toward Rome. The Germans in Italy form a new defensive position on the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caesar_C_line" title="Caesar C line">Caesar C line</a>.</dd>

-The Battle of Odžak ends, concluding all World War II conflicts in Yugoslavia and Europe.

May 26, 1940
-Calais surrenders to the Germans. Operation Dynamo, the Allied evacuation of 340,000 troops from Dunkirk, begins. The move will last until June 3 under ferocious bombardment by the Luftwaffe.
-<dd> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calais" title="Calais">Calais</a> surrenders to the Germans. <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Dynamo" title="Operation Dynamo">Operation Dynamo</a>, the Allied evacuation of 340,000 troops from <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dunkirk,_France" title="Dunkirk, France">Dunkirk</a>, begins. The move will last until June 3 under ferocious bombardment by the Luftwaffe.</dd>
May 26, 1941
-In the North Atlantic, Royal Navy Fairey Swordfish aircraft from the carrier HMS Ark Royal fatally cripple the Bismarck in torpedo attack.
-<dd> In the North Atlantic, Royal Navy <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fairey_Swordfish" title="Fairey Swordfish">Fairey Swordfish</a> aircraft from the carrier <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HMS_Ark_Royal_(91)" title="HMS Ark Royal (91)">HMS <i>Ark Royal</i></a> fatally cripple the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_battleship_Bismarck" title="German battleship Bismarck"><i>Bismarck</i></a> in torpedo attack.</dd>
May 26, 1942
-The Anglo-Soviet Treaty their foreign secretaries agree that no peace will be signed by one without the approval of the other. (An important treaty since Himmler and others will attempt to separate the two nations at the end of the war.)26 Rommel begins a Spring offensive at the Gazala line (west of Tobruk). It opens with "Rommel's Moonlight Ride," a dramatic mechanized dash around 1st Free French Brigade Group positions at Bir Hakeim on the British left (desertward) flank, conducted by moonlight during the night of 26/27 May. In the process Rommel disperses 3rd Indian Motorized Brigade, some six hundred of whom are taken prisoner and then released in the desert, and who will make their way to Bir Hakeim. The offensive lasts well into June and ends with a total victory for Rommel.26 The Free French land on Wallis and Futuna and get rid of the pro-Vichy government there.27 Reinhard Heydrich, head of the Reich Main Security  Office, is fatally wounded in Prague during Operation Anthropoid by Czechoslovak soldiers; he would die on June 4 from his wounds.27 British use American Sherman tanks in attempts to stop Rommel's attacks on the Gazala line.27 USS Yorktown, damaged at the Coral Sea, limps into Pearl Harbor; it is ordered to get repaired and ready as fast as possible for the impending battle.27 In occupied Belgium, wearing of the "yellow badge" becomes compulsory for Jews.29 The Jews in France are ordered to wear the yellow Star of David.29 Japanese forces have large successes south of Shanghai.29 Rommel turns his troops to Bir Hachim on the south edge of the Gazala line; once it is taken, he can move north and destroy the Allied emplacements in the line.30 "The Thousand Bomber Raid" on Cologne, revealing new area bombing techniques.30 USS Yorktown leaves Pearl after hasty repairs and moves to join USS Enterprise for the next expected battle.31 Huge German successes around Kharkov, with envelopment of several Red Army armies.31 Japanese midget subs enter Sydney harbour and sink one support ship; fears of invasion grow.31 So effective has been the use of the Spitfires delivered to Malta in Operation Bowery earlier in the month, that Kesselring has only eighty-three serviceable aircraft left, as opposed to more than four hundred at the peak of Axis air strength earlier in the spring.31 Rommel's offensive has stalled out well short of Tobruk, due to resistance by British 1st Armoured Division and 7th Armoured Division, partially equipped with the new American Sherman tanks. He is also confronted by a long supply line, which must reach around and is under constant threat from the 1st Free French Brigade Group position at Bir Hakeim. He orders two lanes cut through the British minefields which run from Gazala to Bir Hakeim, on either side of fortified positions held by the 150th Brigade of British 50th Infantry Division. He then gathers the bulk of his forces near the outlets of these two lanes, completing the process on the 31st. These tactics serve the triple purpose of shortening his supply line, encircling 150th Brigade, and allowing him to use the British minefields as part of his defences. The area of concentration, promptly nicknamed "the Cauldron" by British Command, will be the focus of the battle for the next few days.

(An important treaty since Himmler and others will attempt to separate the two nations at the end of the war.)<dd>26: Rommel begins a Spring offensive at the Gazala line (west of Tobruk). fears of invasion grow.</dd><dd>31: So effective has been the use of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supermarine_Spitfire" title="Supermarine Spitfire">Spitfires</a> delivered to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Malta_(World_War_II)" title="Siege of Malta (World War II)">Malta</a> in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Bowery" title="Operation Bowery">Operation Bowery</a> earlier in the month, that <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Kesselring" title="Albert Kesselring">Kesselring</a> has only eighty-three serviceable aircraft left, as opposed to more than four hundred at the peak of Axis air strength earlier in the spring.<dd>31: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erwin_Rommel" title="Erwin Rommel">Rommel's</a> offensive has stalled out well short of Tobruk, due to resistance by British <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1st_Armoured_Division_(United_Kingdom)" title="1st Armoured Division (United Kingdom)">1st Armoured Division</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/7th_Armoured_Division_(United_Kingdom)" title="7th Armoured Division (United Kingdom)">7th Armoured Division</a>, partially equipped with the new American <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sherman_tank" title="Sherman tank">Sherman tanks</a>. May 26, 1942
-Rommel begins a Spring offensive at the Gazala line (west of Tobruk). It opens with "Rommel's Moonlight Ride," a dramatic mechanized dash around 1st Free French Brigade Group positions at Bir Hakeim on the British left (desertward) flank, conducted by moonlight during the night of 26/27 May. In the process Rommel disperses 3rd Indian Motorized Brigade, some six hundred of whom are taken prisoner and then released in the desert, and who will make their way to Bir Hakeim. The offensive lasts well into June and ends with a total victory for Rommel.
-<dd> Rommel begins a Spring offensive at the Gazala line (west of Tobruk). It opens with "Rommel's Moonlight Ride," a dramatic mechanized dash around <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1st_Free_French_Division" title="1st Free French Division">1st Free French Brigade Group</a> positions at <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Bir_Hakeim" title="Battle of Bir Hakeim">Bir Hakeim</a> on the British left (desertward) flank, conducted by moonlight during the night of 26/27 May. In the process Rommel disperses <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/3rd_Indian_Motor_Brigade" title="3rd Indian Motor Brigade">3rd Indian Motorized Brigade</a>, some six hundred of whom are taken prisoner and then released in the desert, and who will make their way to Bir Hakeim. The offensive lasts well into June and ends with a total victory for Rommel.</dd>
May 26, 1942
-The Free French land on Wallis and Futuna and get rid of the pro-Vichy government there.
-<dd> The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_France" title="Free France">Free French</a> land on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wallis_and_Futuna" title="Wallis and Futuna">Wallis and Futuna</a> and get rid of the pro-<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vichy_France" title="Vichy France">Vichy</a> government there.</dd>
May 27, 1941
-The German battleship Bismarck is sunk in the North Atlantic by the Royal Navy, after evasive tactics, and a damaged steering system which forced it into an endless series of circular movements. The British forces from the Habbaniya area begin an advance on Baghdad and, within four days, approach the city from the west and from the north. Twelve Italian aircraft arrive at Mosul to join Fliegerführer Irak.
-<dd> The German battleship <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_battleship_Bismarck" title="German battleship Bismarck"><i>Bismarck</i></a> is <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Last_battle_of_the_battleship_Bismarck" title="Last battle of the battleship Bismarck">sunk</a> in the North Atlantic by the Royal Navy, after evasive tactics, and a damaged steering system which forced it into an endless series of circular movements. The British forces from the Habbaniya area begin an advance on Baghdad and, within four days, approach the city from the west and from the north. Twelve <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(1861-1946)" title="Kingdom of Italy (1861-1946)">Italian</a> aircraft arrive at Mosul to join <i>Fliegerführer Irak</i>.</dd>
May 27, 1942
-Reinhard Heydrich, head of the Reich Main Security  Office, is fatally wounded in Prague during Operation Anthropoid by Czechoslovak soldiers; he would die on June 4 from his wounds.27 British use American Sherman tanks in attempts to stop Rommel's attacks on the Gazala line.27 USS Yorktown, damaged at the Coral Sea, limps into Pearl Harbor; it is ordered to get repaired and ready as fast as possible for the impending battle.27 In occupied Belgium, wearing of the "yellow badge" becomes compulsory for Jews.29 The Jews in France are ordered to wear the yellow Star of David.29 Japanese forces have large successes south of Shanghai.29 Rommel turns his troops to Bir Hachim on the south edge of the Gazala line; once it is taken, he can move north and destroy the Allied emplacements in the line.30 "The Thousand Bomber Raid" on Cologne, revealing new area bombing techniques.30 USS Yorktown leaves Pearl after hasty repairs and moves to join USS Enterprise for the next expected battle.31 Huge German successes around Kharkov, with envelopment of several Red Army armies.31 Japanese midget subs enter Sydney harbour and sink one support ship; fears of invasion grow.31 So effective has been the use of the Spitfires delivered to Malta in Operation Bowery earlier in the month, that Kesselring has only eighty-three serviceable aircraft left, as opposed to more than four hundred at the peak of Axis air strength earlier in the spring.31 Rommel's offensive has stalled out well short of Tobruk, due to resistance by British 1st Armoured Division and 7th Armoured Division, partially equipped with the new American Sherman tanks. He is also confronted by a long supply line, which must reach around and is under constant threat from the 1st Free French Brigade Group position at Bir Hakeim. He orders two lanes cut through the British minefields which run from Gazala to Bir Hakeim, on either side of fortified positions held by the 150th Brigade of British 50th Infantry Division. He then gathers the bulk of his forces near the outlets of these two lanes, completing the process on the 31st. These tactics serve the triple purpose of shortening his supply line, encircling 150th Brigade, and allowing him to use the British minefields as part of his defences. The area of concentration, promptly nicknamed "the Cauldron" by British Command, will be the focus of the battle for the next few days.

June 1, 1942
-To further secure his supply lines, Rommel launches an attack on 150th Brigade of British 50th Infantry Division, whose position he has surrounded. Since he is attacking from the east against a position designed to defend against attacks from the west, and since there is scant hope of relief, there is little 150th Brigade can do and they are soon overwhelmed.

June 4, 1942
-[4-7] The Battle of Midway opens with ineffective attacks by land-based American B-17s on the approaching Japanese fleet. Admiral Nagumo, in charge of the Japanese carrier force (Hiryu, Soryu, Akagi, and Kaga) is unable to locate any American aircraft carriers and decides to attack Midway's land-based air defences the first thing the next morning, which in any event is one of his planned tasks.
-<dd> The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Midway" title="Battle of Midway">Battle of Midway</a> opens with ineffective attacks by land-based American <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boeing_B-17_Flying_Fortress" title="Boeing B-17 Flying Fortress">B-17s</a> on the approaching Japanese fleet. Admiral <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chuichi_Nagumo" title="Chuichi Nagumo">Nagumo</a>, in charge of the Japanese carrier force (<a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_aircraft_carrier_Hiryu" title="Japanese aircraft carrier Hiryu"><i>Hiryu</i></a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_aircraft_carrier_Soryu" title="Japanese aircraft carrier Soryu"><i>Soryu</i></a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_aircraft_carrier_Akagi" title="Japanese aircraft carrier Akagi"><i>Akagi</i></a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_aircraft_carrier_Kaga" title="Japanese aircraft carrier Kaga"><i>Kaga</i></a>) is unable to locate any American aircraft carriers and decides to attack Midway's land-based air defences the first thing the next morning, which in any event is one of his planned tasks.</dd>
June 4, 1942
-In the Battle of Midway, the day opens with Admiral Nagumo's attack on the air defences of the island.
-<dd> In the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Midway" title="Battle of Midway">Battle of Midway</a>, the day opens with Admiral <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chuichi_Nagumo" title="Chuichi Nagumo">Nagumo's</a> attack on the air defences of the island.</dd>
June 4, 1942
-A good deal of damage is done and many aircraft destroyed on both sides, but in the end the island's airbase is still functional. Nagumo plans a second attack on the island, and begins refueling and rearming his planes. Meanwhile, attacks are launched from all three American aircraft carriers in the area. Planes from USS Hornet, Yorktown, and Enterprise all find the targets, although most of the planes from Hornet follow an incorrect heading and miss this attack. Torpedo Squadron 8 from Hornet breaks and follows the correct heading. The Devastators of "Torp 8" are all shot down without doing any damage; there is only one survivor, George H. Gay, Jr. of Waco, Texas, who watches the battle unfold from the water. The torpedo attack fails, but draws the Japanese Combat Air Patrol down to low altitude, and they are unable to effectively repel the dive bombers from Yorktown and Enterprise when they arrive. The bombs find the Japanese flight decks crowded with fueling lines and explosive ordnance, and Akagi, Kaga, and Soryu are all soon reduced to blazing hulks, Akagi hit by only one bomb dropped by Lt. Commander Richard Halsey Best; only Hiryu escapes with no hits. Admiral Nagumo shifts his flag from Akagi to another ship, the cruiser Nagara, and orders attacks on the American carriers, one by a group of Aichi D3A dive bombers and a second by Nakajima B5N torpedo bombers. The Japanese planes find Yorktown (thinking Yorktown already sunk, the second attack group assume it must be Enterprise) and damage it so badly that Yorktown must be abandoned. Admiral Fetcher shifts his flag to cruiser Astoria and cedes operational command to Admiral Spruance. The attacks on Yorktown give away Hiryu's continued operations, though, and it is promptly attacked and will sink the next day, Admiral Yamaguchi choosing to go down with it. Of note, Hiryu and the other three destroyed Japanese carriers had participated in the attack on Pearl Harbor.
-<dd> A good deal of damage is done and many aircraft destroyed on both sides, but in the end the island's airbase is still functional. Nagumo plans a second attack on the island, and begins refueling and rearming his planes. Meanwhile, attacks are launched from all three American aircraft carriers in the area. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TBD_Devastator" title="TBD Devastator">Devastators</a> of "Torp 8" are all shot down without doing any damage; there is only one survivor, <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_H._Gay,_Jr." title="George H. Gay, Jr.">George H. Gay, Jr.</a> of Waco, Texas, who watches the battle unfold from the water. The torpedo attack fails, but draws the Japanese Combat Air Patrol down to low altitude, and they are unable to effectively repel the dive bombers from <i>Yorktown</i> and <i>Enterprise</i> when they arrive. The bombs find the Japanese flight decks crowded with fueling lines and explosive ordnance, and <i>Akagi,</i> <i>Kaga,</i> and <i>Soryu</i> are all soon reduced to blazing hulks, <i>Akagi</i> hit by only one bomb dropped by Lt. Commander <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Halsey_Best" title="Richard Halsey Best">Richard Halsey Best</a>; only <i>Hiryu</i> escapes with no hits. Admiral Nagumo shifts his flag from <i>Akagi</i> to another ship, the cruiser <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_cruiser_Nagara" title="Japanese cruiser Nagara"><i>Nagara</i></a>, and orders attacks on the American carriers, one by a group of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aichi_D3A" title="Aichi D3A">Aichi D3A</a> dive bombers and a second by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nakajima_B5N" title="Nakajima B5N">Nakajima B5N</a> torpedo bombers. The Japanese planes find <i>Yorktown</i> (thinking <i>Yorktown</i> already sunk, the second attack group assume it must be <i>Enterprise</i>) and damage it so badly that <i>Yorktown</i> must be abandoned. Admiral <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Jack_Fletcher" title="Frank Jack Fletcher">Fetcher</a> shifts his flag to cruiser <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USS_Astoria_(CA-34)" title="USS Astoria (CA-34)"><i>Astoria</i></a> and cedes operational command to Admiral <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raymond_Spruance" title="Raymond Spruance">Spruance</a>. The attacks on <i>Yorktown</i> give away <i>Hiryu</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> continued operations, though, and it is promptly attacked and will sink the next day, Admiral <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamon_Yamaguchi" title="Tamon Yamaguchi">Yamaguchi</a> choosing to go down with it. Of note, <i>Hiryu</i> and the other three destroyed Japanese carriers had participated in the attack on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a>.</dd>
June 4, 1942
-Reinhard Heydrich, a key architect of the Holocaust, dies in Prague from medical complications that had arisen from injuries suffered from an attempted assassination by Czechoslovak agents one week earlier during Operation Anthropoid.
-<dd> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reinhard_Heydrich" title="Reinhard Heydrich">Reinhard Heydrich</a>, a key architect of the Holocaust, dies in Prague from medical complications that had arisen from injuries suffered from an attempted assassination by Czechoslovak agents one week earlier during <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Anthropoid" title="Operation Anthropoid">Operation Anthropoid</a>.</dd>

June 4, 1944
-Allies enter Rome, one day after the Germans declared it an open city. German troops fall back to the Trasimene Line. Operation Overlord is postponed 24 hours due to high seas. German U-505 was captured by US forces, and towed to Bermuda.
-<dd> Allies enter <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, one day after the Germans declared it an <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open_city" title="Open city">open city</a>. German troops fall back to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trasimene_Line" title="Trasimene Line">Trasimene Line</a>. <i>Operation Overlord</i> is postponed 24 hours due to high seas. German <i>U-505</i> was captured by US forces, and towed to Bermuda.</dd>
June 5, 1942
-At Gazala, British forces of the Eighth Army commanded by General Ritchie launch a major counter-attack against Rommel's forces in the Cauldron. The attack fails, partly because Rommel has already recovered his critical logistics situation and has established an excellent defensive position, but also in large part due to German anti-tank tactics; 32nd Army Tank Brigade, for example, loses 50 of 70 tanks. By early afternoon Rommel is clearly in control of the situation and attacks the British position known as "Knightsbridge" with the Ariete and 21st Panzer divisions. Several British tactical headquarters positions are overrun and command and control of the British forces becomes problematic; as a result, several brigades are stranded in the Cauldron when the British retirement begins. In addition, the British suffer further heavy tank losses.
-<dd> At <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Gazala" title="Battle of Gazala">Gazala</a>, British forces of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Eighth_Army" title="British Eighth Army">Eighth Army</a> commanded by General <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neil_Ritchie" title="Neil Ritchie">Ritchie</a> launch a major counter-attack against <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erwin_Rommel" title="Erwin Rommel">Rommel's</a> forces in the Cauldron. The attack fails, partly because Rommel has already recovered his critical logistics situation and has established an excellent defensive position, but also in large part due to German anti-tank tactics; 32nd Army Tank Brigade, for example, loses 50 of 70 tanks. By early afternoon Rommel is clearly in control of the situation and attacks the British position known as "Knightsbridge" with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Ariete_Armoured_Division" title="Italian Ariete Armoured Division">Ariete</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_21st_Panzer_Division" title="German 21st Panzer Division">21st Panzer</a> divisions. Several British tactical headquarters positions are overrun and command and control of the British forces becomes problematic; as a result, several brigades are stranded in the Cauldron when the British retirement begins. In addition, the British suffer further heavy tank losses.</dd>

June 5, 1944
-Operation Overlord commences when more than 1,000 British bombers drop 5,000 tons of bombs on German gun batteries on the Normandy coast in preparation for D-Day. And the first Allied troops land in Normandy; paratroopers are scattered from Caen southward.  In the Pacific, the U.S. fleet transporting the expeditionary forces for the invasion of Saipan in the Mariana Islands leaves Pearl Harbor.
-<dd> <i>Operation Overlord</i> commences when more than 1,000 <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> bombers drop 5,000 tons of bombs on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> gun batteries on the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a> coast in preparation for <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D-Day" title="D-Day">D-Day</a>. And the first Allied troops land in Normandy; paratroopers are scattered from Caen southward. In the Pacific, the U.S. fleet transporting the expeditionary forces for the invasion of Saipan in the Mariana Islands leaves Pearl Harbor.</dd>

-The Allies agree to divide Germany into four areas of control (American, British, French and Soviet). The U.S. fleet under William Halsey, Jr., suffers widespread damage from a huge Pacific typhoon.

June 7, 1942
-[4-7] The Battle of Midway opens with ineffective attacks by land-based American B-17s on the approaching Japanese fleet. Admiral Nagumo, in charge of the Japanese carrier force (Hiryu, Soryu, Akagi, and Kaga) is unable to locate any American aircraft carriers and decides to attack Midway's land-based air defences the first thing the next morning, which in any event is one of his planned tasks.
-<dd> The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Midway" title="Battle of Midway">Battle of Midway</a> opens with ineffective attacks by land-based American <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boeing_B-17_Flying_Fortress" title="Boeing B-17 Flying Fortress">B-17s</a> on the approaching Japanese fleet. Admiral <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chuichi_Nagumo" title="Chuichi Nagumo">Nagumo</a>, in charge of the Japanese carrier force (<a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_aircraft_carrier_Hiryu" title="Japanese aircraft carrier Hiryu"><i>Hiryu</i></a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_aircraft_carrier_Soryu" title="Japanese aircraft carrier Soryu"><i>Soryu</i></a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_aircraft_carrier_Akagi" title="Japanese aircraft carrier Akagi"><i>Akagi</i></a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_aircraft_carrier_Kaga" title="Japanese aircraft carrier Kaga"><i>Kaga</i></a>) is unable to locate any American aircraft carriers and decides to attack Midway's land-based air defences the first thing the next morning, which in any event is one of his planned tasks.</dd>

-Two convoys set out for Malta, one from Gibraltar (code named 'Harpoon') and the other from Alexandria (code named 'Vigorous'), with desperately needed supplies of food, fuel, and ammunition. The hope is that the Axis will concentrate their attacks on whichever convoy they find first, allowing the other one to get through.
